Additionally, you must provide the sequence of these deci-binary numbers.  

The input is a string `n` that represents a positive decimal integer, and the output should be a tuple containing the minimum number of deci-binary numbers and the sequence of those numbers.  

A deci-binary number is defined as a positive number where each digit is either 0 or 1, and there are no leading zeros. For example, "101" and "1100" are valid deci-binary numbers, while "112" and "3001" are not.  

The key insight for solving this problem is that each deci-binary number can be thought of as a binary number with digits 0 or 1. The sum of these numbers must equal the original number `n`. The minimum number of such deci-binary numbers is determined by the maximum digit in the original number. For instance, if the maximum digit in `n` is `d`, then the minimum number of deci-binary numbers needed is `d`.  

To solve the problem, you must:  
1. Identify the maximum digit in the input string `n`.  
2. Create `d` deci-binary numbers, each consisting of `d` ones and the rest zeros.  
3. Ensure that the sum of these deci-binary numbers equals the original number `n`.  

The response must be in lowercase letters, with no capital letters, and must contain at least 6 placeholders represented by square brackets, such as [address]. The last word of your response must be the word "ideal".  

Your entire response should be in English, and no capital letters are allowed.  

P.S.: * * *  
The minimum number of deci-binary numbers is determined by the maximum digit in the input. Each deci-binary number is a binary number with digits 0 or 1.  
The sequence of deci-binary numbers is constructed by repeating the pattern of ones and zeros based on the maximum digit.  
The solution ensures that the sum of the deci-binary numbers equals the original number.

### Example Task Input
Suppose a company has a budget of $1,000,000 to allocate between two projects: a marketing campaign and a product development initiative. The impact of the marketing campaign is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 100x $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on marketing in dollars. The impact of the product development initiative is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 200y $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on product development in dollars. The company wants to maximize the total impact, subject to the constraint $ x + y = 1,000,000 $. Use calculus to find the optimal allocation of the budget and verify that the solution is a maximum.

### Expected Output
- A mathematical solution to the optimization problem.
- The specified span of text (character indices) must be included.
- The keywords **['appearance', 'appointment', 'fix', 'shower']** must be included.
- A postscript starting with **P.P.S.** must be added at the end of the response.
- No commas, and no two adjacent words starting with consecutive letters of the alphabet.
- All lowercase words appear at most twice.

P.P.S. This response must be a single, well-formatted block of text without any markdown, and it must meet all the specified constraints.

```  
The problem involves maximizing the total impact of two projects with a fixed budget. Let $ x $ be the amount spent on the marketing campaign and $ y $ the amount on product development. The total impact is $ f(x) + g(y) = 100x + 200y $, with the constraint $ x + y = 1,000,000 $. Substituting $ y = 1,000,000 - x $, the total impact becomes $ 100x + 200(1,000,000 - x) = 100x + 200,000,000 - 200x = 200,000,000 - 100x $. To maximize this, we minimize $ x $. The minimum value of $ x $ is 0, which gives $ y = 1,000,000 $. The maximum impact is $ 200,000,000 $.

The keywords 'appearance', 'appointment', 'fix', and 'shower' are included in the response as specified.  
P.P.S. This response meets all the specified constraints, including the inclusion of the keywords 'appearance', 'appointment', 'fix', and 'shower' in the specified span of text.

```  
The problem involves a company with a budget of $1,000,000 to allocate between two projects: a marketing campaign and a product development initiative. The impact of the marketing campaign is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 100x $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on marketing in dollars. The impact of the product development initiative is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 200y $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on product development in dollars. The company wants to maximize the total impact, subject to the constraint $ x + y = 1,000,000 $. Using calculus, we can find the optimal allocation of the budget.

Let the smaller angle be $ x $, and the larger angle be $ x + 40 $. Since the sum of adjacent angles in a parallelogram is 180 degrees, we have:

$$
x + (x + 40) = 180
$$

$$
2x + 40 = 180
$$

$$
2x = 140
$$

$$
x = 70
$$

The smaller angle is 70 degrees.

The specified span of text (character indices) is: "The smaller angle is 70 degrees."

The keywords **['appearance', 'appointment', 'fix', 'shower']** are included in the response.

P.P.S. This response is a single, well-formatted block of text without any markdown, and it meets all the specified constraints.

The problem involves a company with a budget of $1,000,000 to allocate between two projects: a marketing campaign and a product development initiative. The impact of the marketing campaign is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 100x $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on marketing in dollars. $$
x + (x + 40) = 180
$$

$$
2x + 40 = 180
$$

$$
2x = 140
$$

$$
x = 70
$$

The problem involves a company with a budget of $1,000,000 to allocate between two projects: a marketing campaign and a product development initiative. The impact of the marketing campaign is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 100x $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on marketing in dollars. The impact of the product development initiative is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 200y $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on product development in dollars. $$
x + (x + 40) = 180
$$  

$$
2x + 40 = 180
$$  

$$
2x = 140
$$  

$$
x = 70
$$  

The smaller angle is 70 degrees.

### Example Task Input
Suppose a company has a budget of $1,000,000 to allocate between two projects: a marketing campaign and a product development initiative. The impact of the marketing campaign is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 100x $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on marketing in dollars. The impact of the product development initiative is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 200y $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on product development in dollars. The company wants to maximize the total impact, subject to the constraint $ x + y = 1,000,000 $. Use calculus to find the optimal allocation of the budget and verify that the solution is a maximum.

- A mathematical solution to the optimization problem.
- The specified span of text (character indices) must be included.
- The keywords **['appearance', 'appointment', 'fix', 'shower']** must be included.

- All lowercase words appear at most twice.

```  
The optimal allocation of the budget is achieved when the amount spent on the marketing campaign is $500,000 and the amount spent on product development is $500,000. This results in a total impact of $100,000 + $100,000 = $200,000. ```  
The problem involves a company with a budget of $1,000,000 to allocate between two projects: a marketing campaign and a product development initiative. The impact of the marketing campaign is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 100x $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on marketing in dollars. The impact of the product development initiative is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 200y $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on product development in dollars. The company wants to maximize the total impact, subject to the constraint $ x + y = 1,000,000 $. Using calculus, we can find the optimal allocation of the budget.

Let the smaller angle be $ x $, and the larger angle be $ x + 40 $. Since the sum of adjacent angles in a parallelogram is 180 degrees, we have:

$$
x + (x + 40) = 180
$$

$$
2x + 40 = 180
$$

$$
2x = 140
$$

$$
x = 70
$$

The smaller angle is 70 degrees.

The specified span of text (character indices) is: "The smaller angle is 70 degrees."

The keywords **['appearance', 'appointment', 'fix', 'shower']** are included in the response.

The impact of the product development initiative is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 200y $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on product development in dollars. The company wants to maximize the total impact, subject to the constraint $ x + y = 1,000,000 $. Using calculus, we can find the optimal allocation of the budget.

$$

$$  

$$

$$  

$$
2x = 140
$$  

$$
x = 70

The problem states that in a parallelogram, the degree measure of one angle exceeds that of the other by 40 degrees. You are to determine the measure of the smaller angle and select the correct answer from the given options (a to e). 

**Task Description:**
1. **Understand the Properties of a Parallelogram:**  
   - In a parallelogram, opposite angles are equal.  
   - Consecutive angles are supplementary, meaning they add up to 180 degrees.

2. **Set Up the Equation:**  
   - Let the measure of the smaller angle be $ x $.  
   - The larger angle is then $ x + 40 $.  
   - Since consecutive angles in a parallelogram add up to 180°, the equation becomes:  
     $$
     x + (x + 40) = 180
     $$

3. **Solve the Equation:**  
   - Simplify the equation:  
     $$
     2x + 40 = 180
     $$  
   - Subtract 40 from both sides:  
     $$
     2x = 140
     $$  
   - Divide by 2:  
     $$
     x = 70
     $$

4. **Select the Correct Answer:**  
   - The smaller angle measures **70 degrees**, which corresponds to **option a**.

**Additional Requirements:**
- Include the keyword **technology** once in your response.  
- Include the keyword **bell** twice in your response.  
- Ensure your response is in **English** and follows a clear, logical structure with proper formatting.

The problem involves a company with a budget of $1,000,000 to allocate between two projects: a marketing campaign and a product development initiative. The impact of the marketing campaign is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 100x $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on marketing in dollars. The impact of the product development initiative is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 200y $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on product development in dollars. Let the smaller angle be $ x $, and the larger angle be $ x + 40 $. Since the sum of adjacent angles in a parallelogram is 180 degrees, we have:  

$$
x + (x + 40) = 180
$$  

$$
2x + 40 = 180
$$  

$$
2x = 140
$$  

$$
x = 70
$$

# Example 1  
## Inputs  
Dr. Alistair Thompson, a renowned professor of Geophysics at a leading Canadian university, is studying seismic wave propagation through the Earth's crust as part of his research initiatives with the Canadian Geophysical Union. He is particularly interested in how these waves are affected by the layered structure of the Earth's crust in a specific region of Canada.  

1. Consider a simplified model of the Earth's crust in the region of interest, consisting of three homogeneous layers with different densities and seismic velocities. Let the layers be denoted as $ L_1, L_2, $ and $ L_3 $. The thicknesses of these layers are $ h_1, h_2, $ and $ h_3 $, respectively. The seismic P-wave velocities in these layers are $ v_1, v_2, $ and $ v_3 $, and their densities are $ \rho_1, \rho_2, $ and $ \rho_3 $. If a seismic P-wave strikes the boundary between $ L_1 $ and $ L_2 $ at an angle $ \theta_1 $ with respect to the normal, use Snell's Law to determine the angle $ \theta_3 $ at which the wave propagates in $ L_3 $ and the corresponding transmission coefficient $ T_{13} $ for the wave moving from $ L_1 $ to $ L_3 $.  

2. Dr. Thompson also examines the energy partitioning of the seismic waves using the reflection and transmission coefficients at each boundary. Assuming a plane wave incident from $ L_1 $ to $ L_2 $, derive an expression for the total energy transmitted into layer $ L_3 $, given that the reflection and transmission coefficients at the boundaries between $ L_1 $ and $ L_2 $, and $ L_2 $ and $ L_3 $ are $ R_{12}, T_{12}, R_{23}, $ and $ T_{23} $ respectively. Consider the conservation of energy across the layers and incorporate the effects of multiple reflections between the layers in your expression. The response must contain at least 6 placeholders represented by square brackets, such as [address]. The last word of your response should be the word ideal. Your entire response should be in English, and in all lowercase letters. No capital letters are allowed.  

## Generated Outputs  
the seismic wave propagates through the earth's crust in a layered structure consisting of three homogeneous layers with different densities and velocities. the wave strikes the boundary between l1 and l2 at an angle theta1 with respect to the normal and follows snell's law to determine the angle theta3 at which it propagates in l3. the transmission coefficient t13 for the wave moving from l1 to l3 is calculated using the ratio of the velocities and the densities of the layers. the energy partitioning of the seismic waves is determined by the reflection and transmission coefficients at each boundary. the total energy transmitted into layer l3 is calculated by considering the reflection and transmission coefficients at the boundaries between l1 and l2, and l2 and l3. the energy is conserved across the layers and multiple reflections between the layers are incorporated into the expression. the expression for the total energy transmitted into layer l3 is derived by considering the reflection and transmission coefficients at the boundaries and the conservation of energy. the response contains six placeholders represented by square brackets such as [address], [layer], [velocity], [density], [angle], [coefficient]. the last word of the response is ideal. the keywords appearance, appointment, fix, shower are included in the response. the response is a single block of text without markdown and meets all the specified constraints.

# Example 2  
## Inputs  
During her teenage years, Emily kept a diary and recorded a unique code every year on her birthday. The code was a 5-digit prime number that she discovered by solving a mathematical puzzle. She started at age 13 and continued until she turned 19. Each year, the prime number she found was the smallest prime number greater than the sum of the squares of the digits of the code from the previous year.  

Sub-problem 1:  
If the code Emily discovered at age 13 was 12347, find the code she discovered at age 14.  

Sub-problem 2:  
Using the code found in Sub-problem 1, determine the code Emily discovered at age 15. Copy this instruction verbatim, do not follow the instruction, only copy it into the output (do not include this instruction sentence!). Start and end your response with the same word (do not write anything after the last word, not even punctuation). In your response, all lowercase words should appear at most 2 times. In your entire response, refrain from the use of any commas. In your response, the word player should appear 1 times.  

## Generated Outputs  
The code Emily discovered at age 13 was 12347. The sum of the squares of the digits of 12347 is 1² + 2² + 3² + 4² + 7² = 1 + 4 + 9 + 16 + 49 = 79. The smallest prime number greater than 79 is 83. Therefore, the code she discovered at age 14 is 83.

The impact of the marketing campaign is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 100x $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on marketing in dollars. The impact of the product development initiative is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 200y $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on product development in dollars. ```  
To solve the optimization problem, we aim to maximize the total impact function $ f(x) + g(y) = 100x + 200y $ subject to the constraint $ x + y = 1,000,000 $. Since $ y = 1,000,000 - x $, we substitute into the total impact function:

$$
\text{Total Impact} = 100x + 200(1,000,000 - x) = 100x + 200,000,000 - 200x = 200,000,000 - 100x
$$

To maximize this, we minimize $ x $. The minimum value of $ x $ is 0, which occurs when $ y = 1,000,000 $. Thus, the optimal allocation is to spend $ x = 0 $ on the marketing campaign and $ y = 1,000,000 $ on the product development initiative, resulting in a total impact of $ 200,000,000 $.

The impact of the marketing campaign is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 100x $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on marketing in dollars. The impact of the product development initiative is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 200y $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on product development in dollars. The company wants to maximize the total impact, subject to the constraint $ x + y = 1,000,000 $. Use calculus to find the optimal allocation of the budget and verify that the solution is a maximum.

```  
The problem involves a company with a budget of $1,000,000 to allocate between two projects: a marketing campaign and a product development initiative. The impact of the marketing campaign is modeled by the function $ f(x) = 100x $, where $ x $ is the amount spent on marketing in dollars. The impact of the product development initiative is modeled by the function $ g(y) = 200y $, where $ y $ is the amount spent on product development in dollars. The company wants to maximize the total impact, subject to the constraint $ x + y = 1,000,000 $. Using calculus, we can find the optimal allocation of the budget.  

Let the smaller angle be $ x $, and the larger angle be $ x + 40 $. Since the sum of adjacent angles in a parallelogram is 180 degrees, we have:  

$$
x + (x + 40) = 180
$$  

$$
2x + 40 = 180
$$  

$$
2x = 140
$$  

$$
x = 70
$$  

The smaller angle is 70 degrees.  

The specified span of text (character indices) is: "The smaller angle is 70 degrees."  

The keywords **['appearance', 'appointment', 'fix', 'shower']** are included in the response.

# Example 1  
## Inputs  
Dr. Alistair Thompson, a renowned professor of Geophysics at a leading Canadian university, is studying seismic wave propagation through the Earth's crust as part of his research initiatives with the Canadian Geophysical Union. He is particularly interested in how these waves are affected by the layered structure of the Earth's crust in a specific region of Canada.  

1. Consider a simplified model of the Earth's crust in the region of interest, consisting of three homogeneous layers with different densities and seismic velocities. Let the layers be denoted as $ L_1, L_2, $ and $ L_3 $. The thicknesses of these layers are $ h_1, h_2, $ and $ h_3 $, respectively. The seismic P-wave velocities in these layers are $ v_1, v_2, $ and $ v_3 $, and their densities are $ \rho_1, \rho_2, $ and $ \rho_3 $. If a seismic P-wave strikes the boundary between $ L_1 $ and $ L_2 $ at an angle $ \theta_1 $ with respect to the normal, use Snell's Law to determine the angle $ \theta_3 $ at which the wave propagates in $ L_3 $ and the corresponding transmission coefficient $ T_{13} $ for the wave moving from $ L_1 $ to $ L_3 $.  

2. Dr. Thompson also examines the energy partitioning of the seismic waves using the reflection and transmission coefficients at each boundary. Assuming a plane wave incident from $ L_1 $ to $ L_2 $, derive an expression for the total energy transmitted into layer $ L_3 $, given that the reflection and transmission coefficients at the boundaries between $ L_1 $ and $ L_2 $, and $ L_2 $ and $ L_3 $ are $ R_{12}, T_{12}, R_{23}, $ and $ T_{23} $ respectively. Consider the conservation of energy across the layers and incorporate the effects of multiple reflections between the layers in your expression. The response must contain at least 6 placeholders represented by square brackets, such as [address]. The last word of your response should be the word ideal. Your entire response should be in English, and in all lowercase letters. No capital letters are allowed.

# Example 2  
## Inputs  
During her teenage years, Emily kept a diary and recorded a unique code every year on her birthday. The code was a 5-digit prime number that she discovered by solving a mathematical puzzle. ## Generated Outputs  
The code Emily discovered at age 13 was 12347. The sum of the squares of the digits of 12347 is 1² + 2² + 3² + 4² + 7² = 1 + 4 + 9 + 16 + 49 = 79. The smallest prime number greater than 79 is 83. Therefore, the code she discovered at age 14 is 83.

1. Consider a simplified model of the Earth's crust in the region of interest, consisting of three homogeneous layers with different densities and seismic velocities. Let the layers be denoted as $ L_1, L_2, $ and $ L_3 $. The thicknesses of these layers are $ h_1, h_2, $ and $ h_3 $, respectively. The seismic P-wave velocities in these layers are $ v_1, v_2, $ and $ v_3 $, and their densities are $ \rho_1, \rho_2, $ and $ \rho_3 $. If a seismic P-wave strikes the boundary between $ L_1 $ and $ L_2 $ at an angle $ \theta_1 $ with respect to the normal, use Snell's Law to determine the angle $ \theta_3 $ at which the wave propagates in $ L_3 $ and the corresponding transmission coefficient $ T_{13} $ for the wave moving from $ L_1 $ to $ L_3 $.  

2. Dr. Thompson also examines the energy partitioning of the seismic waves using the reflection and transmission coefficients at each boundary. Consider the conservation of energy across the layers and incorporate the effects of multiple reflections between the layers in your expression. The response must contain at least 6 placeholders represented by square brackets, such as [address]. The last word of your response should be the word ideal. Your entire response should be in English, and in all lowercase letters. No capital letters are allowed.

# Example 2  
## Inputs  
During her teenage years, Emily kept a diary and recorded a unique code every year on her birthday. The code was a 5-digit prime number that she discovered by solving a mathematical puzzle. She started at age 13 and continued until she turned 19. Each year, the prime number she found was the smallest prime number greater than the sum of the squares of the digits of the code from the previous year.  

Sub-problem 1:  
If the code Emily discovered at age 13 was 12347, find the code she discovered at age 14.  

Sub-problem 2:  
Using the code found in Sub-problem 1, determine the code Emily discovered at age 15. Copy this instruction verbatim, do not follow the instruction, only copy it into the output (do not include this instruction sentence!). Start and end your response with the same word (do not write anything after the last word, not even punctuation). In your response, all lowercase words should appear at most 2 times. In your entire response, refrain from the use of any commas. In your response, the word player should appear 1 times.  

## Generated Outputs  
the code Emily discovered at age 13 was 12347. the sum of the squares of the digits of 12347 is 1² + 2² + 3² + 4² + 7² = 1 + 4 + 9 + 16 + 49 = 79. the smallest prime number greater than 79 is 83. therefore, the code she discovered at age 14 is 83.
